<ul style="line-height:100%; margin-left:1.35em;padding-left:0"><li>
<a href="/wiki/Atlantic%E2%80%93Congo_languages" title="Atlantic–Congo languages">Atlantic–Congo</a><ul style="line-height:100%;margin-left:0.45em;padding-left:0;"><li><a href="/wiki/Volta-Congo" class="mw-redirect" title="Volta-Congo">Volta-Congo</a><ul style="line-height:100%;margin-left:0.45em;padding-left:0;"><li><a href="/wiki/Benue%E2%80%93Congo_languages" title="Benue–Congo languages">Benue–Congo</a><ul style="line-height:100%;margin-left:0.45em;padding-left:0;"><li><a href="/wiki/Bantoid_languages" title="Bantoid languages">Bantoid</a><ul style="line-height:100%;margin-left:0.45em;padding-left:0;"><li><a href="/wiki/Southern_Bantoid" class="mw-redirect" title="Southern Bantoid">Southern Bantoid</a><ul style="line-height:100%;margin-left:0.45em;padding-left:0;"><li><a href="/wiki/Bantu_languages" title="Bantu languages">Bantu</a> (<a href="/wiki/Guthrie_classification_of_Bantu_languages#Zone_N" title="Guthrie classification of Bantu languages">Zone N</a>)<ul style="line-height:100%;margin-left:0.45em;padding-left:0;"><li><a href="/wiki/Nyasa_languages" title="Nyasa languages">Nyasa</a><ul style="line-height:100%;margin-left:0.45em;padding-left:0;"><li><b>Tumbuka</b></li></ul></li></ul></li></ul></li></ul></li></ul></li></ul></li></ul></li></ul></div></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label" style="white-space:nowrap;padding-right:0.65em;"><div style="display: inline-block; line-height: 1.2em; padding: .1em 0;"><span class="wrap"><a href="/wiki/Writing_system" title="Writing system">Writing system</a></span></div></th><td class="infobox-data" style="line-height:1.3em;"><style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1126788409">.mw-parser-output .plainlist ol,.mw-parser-output .plainlist ul{line-height:inherit;list-style:none;margin:0;padding:0}.mw-parser-output .plainlist ol li,.mw-parser-output .plainlist ul li{margin-bottom:0}</style><div class="plainlist">
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Latin_script" title="Latin script">Latin script</a> (<a href="#Orthography">Roman alphabet</a>)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Mwangwego_script" title="Mwangwego script">Mwangwego script</a></li></ul>
</div></td></tr><tr><th colspan="2" class="infobox-header" style="color: black; background-color:  #ffddaa;">Official status</th></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label" style="white-space:nowrap;padding-right:0.65em;"><div style="display: inline-block; line-height: 1.2em; padding: .1em 0;">Recognised minority<br />language&#160;in</div></th><td class="infobox-data" style="line-height:1.3em;"><div style="vertical-align:middle;"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1126788409"><div class="plainlist">
<ul><li><span class="flagicon"><span class="mw-image-border" typeof="mw:File"><span><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/Flag_of_Malawi.svg/23px-Flag_of_Malawi.svg.png" decoding="async" width="23" height="15" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/Flag_of_Malawi.svg/35px-Flag_of_Malawi.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/Flag_of_Malawi.svg/45px-Flag_of_Malawi.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="900" data-file-height="600" /></span></span>&#160;</span><a href="/wiki/Malawi" title="Malawi">Malawi</a></li>
<li><span class="flagicon"><span class="mw-image-border" typeof="mw:File"><span><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/Flag_of_Zambia.svg/23px-Flag_of_Zambia.svg.png" decoding="async" width="23" height="15" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/Flag_of_Zambia.svg/35px-Flag_of_Zambia.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/Flag_of_Zambia.svg/45px-Flag_of_Zambia.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="900" data-file-height="600" /></span></span>&#160;</span><a href="/wiki/Zambia" title="Zambia">Zambia</a></li>
<li><span class="flagicon"><span class="mw-image-border" typeof="mw:File"><span><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Flag_of_Tanzania.svg/23px-Flag_of_Tanzania.svg.png" decoding="async" width="23" height="15" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Flag_of_Tanzania.svg/35px-Flag_of_Tanzania.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Flag_of_Tanzania.svg/45px-Flag_of_Tanzania.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="900" data-file-height="600" /></span></span>&#160;</span><a href="/wiki/Tanzania" title="Tanzania">Tanzania</a></li></ul>
</div></div></td></tr><tr><th colspan="2" class="infobox-header" style="color: black; background-color:  #ffddaa;">Language codes</th></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label" style="white-space:nowrap;padding-right:0.65em;"><span class="nowrap"><a href="/wiki/ISO_639-2" title="ISO 639-2">ISO 639-2</a></span></th><td class="infobox-data" style="line-height:1.3em;"><code><span class="plainlinks"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.loc.gov/standards/iso639-2/php/langcodes_name.php?code_ID=462">tum</a></span></code></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label" style="white-space:nowrap;padding-right:0.65em;"><span class="nowrap"><a href="/wiki/ISO_639-3" title="ISO 639-3">ISO 639-3</a></span></th><td class="infobox-data" style="line-height:1.3em;"><code><a href="https://iso639-3.sil.org/code/tum" class="extiw" title="iso639-3:tum">tum</a></code></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label" style="white-space:nowrap;padding-right:0.65em;"><i><a href="/wiki/Glottolog" title="Glottolog">Glottolog</a></i></th><td class="infobox-data" style="line-height:1.3em;"><code><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://glottolog.org/resource/languoid/id/tumb1250">tumb1250</a></code></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label" style="white-space:nowrap;padding-right:0.65em;"><div style="display: inline-block; line-height: 1.2em; padding: .1em 0;"><span class="wrap"><a href="/wiki/Guthrie_classification_of_Bantu_languages" title="Guthrie classification of Bantu languages">Guthrie code</a></span></div></th><td class="infobox-data" style="line-height:1.3em;"><code>N.21</code><sup id="cite_ref-Guthrie_2-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Guthrie-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label" style="white-space:nowrap;padding-right:0.65em;"><a href="/wiki/Linguasphere_Observatory" title="Linguasphere Observatory">Linguasphere</a></th><td class="infobox-data" style="line-height:1.3em;"><code><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://linguasphere.info/?page=linguascale&amp;linguacode=99-AUS-wc">99-AUS-wc</a> (+ chi-Kamanga) incl. varieties 99-AUS-wca...-wcl</code></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>The <b>Tumbuka language</b> is a <a href="/wiki/Bantu_languages" title="Bantu languages">Bantu language</a> which is spoken in <a href="/wiki/Malawi" title="Malawi">Malawi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Zambia" title="Zambia">Zambia</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Tanzania" title="Tanzania">Tanzania</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Michigan_3-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Michigan-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> It is also known by the autonym <span title="Tumbuka-language text"><i lang="tum">Chitumbuka</i></span> also spelled <span title="Tumbuka-language text"><i lang="tum">Citumbuka</i></span> — the <i>chi-</i> prefix in front of <i>Tumbuka</i> means <i>"in the manner of"</i>, and is understood in this case to mean "the language of the <a href="/wiki/Tumbuka_people" title="Tumbuka people">Tumbuka people</a>". Tumbuka belongs to the same language group (<a href="/wiki/Guthrie_classification_of_Bantu_languages#Zone_N" title="Guthrie classification of Bantu languages">Guthrie Zone N</a>) as <a href="/wiki/Chewa_language" title="Chewa language">Chewa</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The World Almanac (1998) estimated that there were approximately 2,080,000  Tumbuka speakers in 1998, though other sources estimated a much smaller number. The majority of Tumbuka speakers are said to live in Malawi.<sup id="cite_ref-Michigan_3-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Michigan-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> Tumbuka is the most widely spoken of the languages of Northern Malawi, especially in the <a href="/wiki/Rumphi" title="Rumphi">Rumphi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mzuzu" title="Mzuzu">Mzuzu</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mzimba" title="Mzimba">Mzimba</a> and <a href="/wiki/Karonga_District" title="Karonga District">Karonga</a> districts.<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>There are substantial differences between the form of Tumbuka spoken in urban areas of Malawi (which borrows some words from <a href="/wiki/Swahili_language" title="Swahili language">Swahili</a> and <a href="/wiki/Chewa_language" title="Chewa language">Chewa</a>) and the "village" or "deep" Tumbuka spoken in villages. The <a href="/wiki/Rumphi" title="Rumphi">Rumphi</a> variant is often regarded as the most "linguistically pure", and is sometimes called "real Tumbuka".<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Mzimba" title="Mzimba">Mzimba</a> dialect has been strongly influenced by <a href="/wiki/Zulu_language" title="Zulu language">Zulu</a> (chiNgoni),<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> even so far as to have <a href="/wiki/Click_consonant" title="Click consonant">clicks</a> in words like <span title="Tumbuka-language text"><i lang="tum">chitha</i></span> <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA" title="Help:IPA">&#91;ʇʰitʰa&#93;</a></span> "urinate", which do not occur in other dialects.
</p><p>Throughout the history of Malawi, only Tumbuka and Chewa have at one time or another been the primary dominant language used by government officials. However, the Tumbuka language suffered a lot  during the rule of President <a href="/wiki/Hastings_Banda" title="Hastings Banda">Hastings Kamuzu Banda</a>, since in 1968 as a result of his one-nation, one-language policy it lost its status as an official language in Malawi. As a result, Tumbuka was removed from the school curriculum, the national radio, and the print media.<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> With the advent of multi-party democracy in 1994, Tumbuka programmes were started again on the radio, but the number of books and other publications in Tumbuka remains low.<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<meta property="mw:PageProp/toc" />
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Orthography">Orthography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tumbuka_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Orthography"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<figure typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><span><video id="mwe_player_0" poster="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9f/WIKITONGUES-Temwa_Speaking_Tumbuka_-_free_to_use_file_under_Wikipedia_policies.webm/326px--WIKITONGUES-Temwa_Speaking_Tumbuka_-_free_to_use_file_under_Wikipedia_policies.webm.jpg" controls="" preload="none" class="mw-file-element" width="326" height="183" data-durationhint="347" data-mwtitle="WIKITONGUES-Temwa_Speaking_Tumbuka_-_free_to_use_file_under_Wikipedia_policies.webm" data-mwprovider="wikimediacommons" resource="/wiki/File:WIKITONGUES-Temwa_Speaking_Tumbuka_-_free_to_use_file_under_Wikipedia_policies.webm"><source src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/9/9f/WIKITONGUES-Temwa_Speaking_Tumbuka_-_free_to_use_file_under_Wikipedia_policies.webm" type="video/webm; codecs=&quot;vp8, vorbis&quot;" data-width="1280" data-height="720" /><source src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/transcoded/9/9f/WIKITONGUES-Temwa_Speaking_Tumbuka_-_free_to_use_file_under_Wikipedia_policies.webm/WIKITONGUES-Temwa_Speaking_Tumbuka_-_free_to_use_file_under_Wikipedia_policies.webm.m3u8" type="application/vnd.apple.mpegurl" data-transcodekey="m3u8" data-width="0" data-height="0" /></video></span><figcaption>Temwa Speaking basic Tumbuka greetings.</figcaption></figure>
<p>Two systems of writing Tumbuka are in use: the traditional spelling (used for example in the Chitumbuka version of Wikipedia and in the newspaper <span title="Tumbuka-language text"><i lang="tum">Fuko</i></span>), in which words such as <span title="Tumbuka-language text"><i lang="tum">banthu</i></span> 'people' and <span title="Tumbuka-language text"><i lang="tum">chaka</i></span> 'year' are written with 'b' and 'ch', and the new official spelling (used for example in the Citumbuka dictionary published online by the Centre for Language Studies and in the online Bible), in which the same words are written with 'ŵ' and 'c', e.g. <i>ŵanthu</i> and <i>caka</i>. (The sound 'ŵ' is a closely rounded [w] pronounced with the tongue in the close-i position.)<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> There is some uncertainty over where to write 'r' and where 'l', e.g. <span title="Tumbuka-language text"><i lang="tum">cakulya</i></span> (Dictionary) or <span title="Tumbuka-language text"><i lang="tum">cakurya</i></span> (Bible) 'food'. (In fact [l] and [r] are <a href="/wiki/Allophones" class="mw-redirect" title="Allophones">allophones</a> of the same <a href="/wiki/Phoneme" title="Phoneme">phoneme</a>.) There is also hesitation between the spellings 'sk' and 'sy' (both <span title="Tumbuka-language text"><i lang="tum">miskombe</i></span> and <span title="Tumbuka-language text"><i lang="tum">misyombe</i></span> ('bamboo') are found in the Citumbuka dictionary).<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Phonology">Phonology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tumbuka_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Phonology"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Vowels">Vowels</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tumbuka_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Vowels"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The same vowels <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/a/</span>, <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ɛ/</span>, <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/i/</span>, <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ɔ/</span>, <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/u/</span> and syllabic <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/m̩/</span> are found in Tumbuka as in the neighbouring language <a href="/wiki/Chewa_language" title="Chewa language">Chewa</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><span><audio id="mwe_player_1" controls="" preload="none" class="mw-file-element" width="220" style="width:220px;" data-durationhint="13" data-mwtitle="Monile.ogg" data-mwprovider="wikimediacommons" resource="/wiki/File:Monile.ogg"><source src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/transcoded/f/fc/Monile.ogg/Monile.ogg.mp3" type="audio/mpeg" data-transcodekey="mp3" data-width="0" data-height="0" /><source src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/f/fc/Monile.ogg" type="audio/ogg; codecs=&quot;vorbis&quot;" data-width="0" data-height="0" /></audio></span><figcaption>Tumbuka greeting "Monile" which means "Hello".</figcaption></figure>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Consonants">Consonants</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tumbuka_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Consonants"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Tumbuka consonants are also similar to those of the neighbouring <a href="/wiki/Chewa_language" title="Chewa language">Chewa</a>, but with certain differences. The continuant sounds <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ɣ/</span>, <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/β/</span> and <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/h/</span>, which are absent or marginal in Chewa, are common in Tumbuka. Also common are the palatalised sounds <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/vʲ/</span>, <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/fʲ/</span>, <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/bʲ/</span>, <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/pʲ/</span>, <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/skʲ/</span>, <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/zgʲ/</span>, and <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ɽʲ/</span>. In Tumbuka there are no affricates such as Chichewa <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/psʲ/</span>, <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/bzʲ/</span>, <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/t͡s/</span>, <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/d͡z/</span>. The sounds <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/s/</span> and <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/z/</span> are never nasalised in Tumbuka, so that Chewa <span title="Chichewa-language text"><i lang="ny">nsómba</i></span> ('fish') = Tumbuka <span title="Tumbuka-language text"><i lang="tum">somba</i></span>. The sound <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ʃ/</span> is found only in foreign words such as <span title="Tumbuka-language text"><i lang="tum">shati</i></span> ('shirt') and <span title="Tumbuka-language text"><i lang="tum">shuga</i></span> ('sugar'). Tumbuka <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ɽ/</span> sometimes corresponds to Chewa <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/d/</span>, for example Chewa <span title="Chichewa-language text"><i lang="ny">kudwala</i></span> 'to be ill' = Tumbuka <span title="Tumbuka-language text"><i lang="tum">kulwala</i></span>, Chewa <span title="Chichewa-language text"><i lang="ny">kudya</i></span> 'to eat' = Tumbuka <span title="Tumbuka-language text"><i lang="tum">kulya</i></span>. The pronunciation of "sk" and "zg" varies according to dialect.
</p><p>Tumbuka consonants are frequently either palatalised (i.e. followed by /y/) or rounded (i.e. followed by /w/.) Some of them can also be preceded by a <a href="/wiki/Homorganic_consonant" title="Homorganic consonant">homorganic</a> nasal (/n/, /ng'/ or /m/). The possible consonant combinations are shown in the table below:
</p>

<li id="cite_note-15"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-15">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Only in the word <span title="Tumbuka-language text"><i lang="tum">ndyali</i></span>.</span>
</li>
</ol></div></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tone">Tone</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tumbuka_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Tone"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>One of the main differences between Chewa and Tumbuka is that Chewa is a <a href="/wiki/Tone_(linguistics)" title="Tone (linguistics)">tonal</a> language, whereas in Tumbuka there are no distinctions of tone between one word and another.
</p><p>Tumbuka has a <a href="/wiki/Tone_(linguistics)" title="Tone (linguistics)">tonal</a> accent but in a very limited way, in that every word, spoken in isolation, has the same falling tone on the penultimate syllable (which also coincides with stress).<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> It is therefore not possible in Tumbuka to contrast two different words or two different tenses tonally, as it is in <a href="/wiki/Chewa_language" title="Chewa language">Chichewa</a> and other Bantu languages. However, this penultimate falling tone occurs not on every word, but only on the last word of a phonological phrase; e.g. in the following sentence, only the second word has a tone, the first being toneless:<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<ul><li><span title="Tumbuka-language text"><i lang="tum">ti-ku-phika sî:ma</i></span> 'we are cooking porridge'</li></ul>
<p>A greater variety of tonal patterns is found in the <a href="/wiki/Ideophone" title="Ideophone">ideophones</a> (expressive words) of Tumbuka; for example Low (<span title="Tumbuka-language text"><i lang="tum">yoyoyo</i></span> 'disintegrating into small pieces'), High (<span title="Tumbuka-language text"><i lang="tum">fyá:</i></span> 'swooping low (of birds)'), High-Low (<span title="Tumbuka-language text"><i lang="tum">phúli</i></span> 'sound of thing bursting'), and Low-High (<span title="Tumbuka-language text"><i lang="tum">yií</i></span> 'sudden disappearance'), etc.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Intonational tones are also used in Tumbuka; for example, in yes–no questions there is often a High-Low fall on the final syllable of the question:<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<ul><li><span title="Tumbuka-language text"><i lang="tum">ku-limirâ-so ngô:mâ?</i></span> 'are you also weeding the maize?'</li></ul>
<p>There does not seem to be any consistent, direct correlation between tone in Tumbuka and <a href="/wiki/Focus_(linguistics)" title="Focus (linguistics)">focus</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Nouns">Nouns</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tumbuka_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Nouns"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Noun_classes">Noun classes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tumbuka_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Noun classes"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>As is usual with Bantu languages, Tumbuka nouns are grouped into different noun classes according to their singular and plural prefixes. Each class of noun has its own adjective, pronoun, and verb agreements, known as 'concords'. Where the agreements disagree with the prefix, the agreements take precedence in deciding the class of noun. For example, the noun <span title="Tumbuka-language text"><i lang="tum">katundu</i></span> 'possessions', despite having the prefix <i>ka-</i>, is placed in class 1, since one says <span title="Tumbuka-language text"><i lang="tum">katundu uyu</i></span> 'these possessions' using the class 1 demonstrative <span title="Tumbuka-language text"><i lang="tum">uyu</i></span>. Malawians themselves (e.g. in the University of Malawi's Citumbuka dictionary) refer to the noun classes by traditional names such as "Mu-Ŵa-"; Bantu specialists, however, refer to the classes by numbers (1/2 etc.) corresponding to the noun-classes of other Bantu languages. Occasionally nouns do not correspond to the classes below, e.g. <span title="Tumbuka-language text"><i lang="tum">fumu</i></span> 'chief' (class 9) irregularly has a plural <i>mafumu</i> in class 6.
</p><p><b>Class 1/2 (Mu-Ŵa-)</b>
</p><p>Some nouns in this class lack the prefix Mu-:
</p>
<ul><li><span title="Tumbuka-language text"><i lang="tum">Munthu</i></span> pl. <span title="Tumbuka-language text"><i lang="tum">ŵanthu (banthu)</i></span> = person</li>
<li><span title="Tumbuka-language text"><i lang="tum">Muzungu</i></span> pl. <span title="Tumbuka-language text"><i lang="tum">ŵazungu (bazungu)</i></span> = foreigner, white man</li>
<li><span title="Tumbuka-language text"><i lang="tum">Mwana</i></span> pl. <span title="Tumbuka-language text"><i lang="tum">ŵana (bana)</i></span> = child</li>
<li><span title="Tumbuka-language text"><i lang="tum">Bulu</i></span> pl. <span title="Tumbuka-language text"><i lang="tum">ŵabulu</i></span> = donkey</li>
<li><span title="Tumbuka-language text"><i lang="tum">Sibweni</i></span> pl. <span title="Tumbuka-language text"><i lang="tum">ŵasibweni</i></span> = maternal uncle</li>
<li><span title="Tumbuka-language text"><i lang="tum">Katundu</i></span> (no pl.) = goods, possessions</li></ul>
<p><b>Class 3/4 (Mu-Mi-)</b>
</p>
<ul><li><span title="Tumbuka-language text"><i lang="tum">Mutu</i></span> pl. <span title="Tumbuka-language text"><i lang="tum">mitu</i></span> = head</li>
<li><span title="Tumbuka-language text"><i lang="tum">Mkuyu</i></span> pl. <span title="Tumbuka-language text"><i lang="tum">mikuyu</i></span> = fig-tree</li>
<li><span title="Tumbuka-language text"><i lang="tum">Moyo</i></span> pl. <span title="Tumbuka-language text"><i lang="tum">miyoyo</i></span> = life</li>
<li><span title="Tumbuka-language text"><i lang="tum">Mtima</i></span> pl. <span title="Tumbuka-language text"><i lang="tum">mitima</i></span> = heart</li></ul>
<p><b>Class 5/6 (Li-Ma-)</b>
</p>
<ul><li><span title="Tumbuka-language text"><i lang="tum">Bele (bhele</i></span> pl. <span title="Tumbuka-language text"><i lang="tum">mabele (mabhele)</i></span> = breast</li>
<li><span title="Tumbuka-language text"><i lang="tum">Boma (bhoma)</i></span> pl. <span title="Tumbuka-language text"><i lang="tum">maboma (mabhoma)</i></span> = government, district</li>
<li><span title="Tumbuka-language text"><i lang="tum">Botolo (bhotolo)</i></span> pl. <span title="Tumbuka-language text"><i lang="tum">mabotolo (mabhotolo)</i></span> = bottle</li>
<li><span title="Tumbuka-language text"><i lang="tum">Fuko</i></span> pl. <span title="Tumbuka-language text"><i lang="tum">mafuko</i></span> = tribe, nation</li>
<li><span title="Tumbuka-language text"><i lang="tum">Jiso</i></span> pl. <span title="Tumbuka-language text"><i lang="tum">maso</i></span> = eye</li>
<li><span title="Tumbuka-language text"><i lang="tum">Maji</i></span> (no singular) = water</li>
<li><span title="Tumbuka-language text"><i lang="tum">Phiri</i></span> pl. <span title="Tumbuka-language text"><i lang="tum">mapiri</i></span> = hill</li>
<li><span title="Tumbuka-language text"><i lang="tum">Suzgo</i></span> pl. <span title="Tumbuka-language text"><i lang="tum">masuzgo</i></span> = problem, trouble</li>
<li><span title="Tumbuka-language text"><i lang="tum">Woko</i></span> pl. <span title="Tumbuka-language text"><i lang="tum">mawoko</i></span> = hand</li></ul>
<p><b>Class 7/8 (Ci-Vi-)</b>
</p>
<ul><li><span title="Tumbuka-language text"><i lang="tum">Caka (chaka)</i></span> pl. <span title="Tumbuka-language text"><i lang="tum">vyaka</i></span> = year</li>
<li><span title="Tumbuka-language text"><i lang="tum">Caro (charo)</i></span> pl. <span title="Tumbuka-language text"><i lang="tum">vyaro</i></span> = country, land</li>
<li><span title="Tumbuka-language text"><i lang="tum">Ciŵeto (chibeto)</i></span> pl. <span title="Tumbuka-language text"><i lang="tum">viŵeto (vibeto)</i></span> = farm animal</li>
<li><span title="Tumbuka-language text"><i lang="tum">Cidakwa (chidakwa)</i></span> pl. <span title="Tumbuka-language text"><i lang="tum">vidakwa</i></span> = drunkard</li>
<li><span title="Tumbuka-language text"><i lang="tum">Cikoti (chikoti)</i></span> pl. <span title="Tumbuka-language text"><i lang="tum">vikoti</i></span> = whip</li></ul>
<p><b>Class 9/10 (Yi-Zi-)</b>
</p>
<ul><li><span title="Tumbuka-language text"><i lang="tum">Mbale</i></span> pl. <span title="Tumbuka-language text"><i lang="tum">mbale (mambale)</i></span> = plate</li>
<li><span title="Tumbuka-language text"><i lang="tum">Ndalama</i></span> pl. <span title="Tumbuka-language text"><i lang="tum">ndalama</i></span> = money</li>
<li><span title="Tumbuka-language text"><i lang="tum">Njelwa</i></span> pl. <span title="Tumbuka-language text"><i lang="tum">njelwa</i></span> = brick</li>
<li><span title="Tumbuka-language text"><i lang="tum">Nkhuku</i></span> pl. <span title="Tumbuka-language text"><i lang="tum">nkhuku</i></span> = chicken</li>
<li><span title="Tumbuka-language text"><i lang="tum">Somba</i></span> pl. <span title="Tumbuka-language text"><i lang="tum">somba</i></span> = fish</li></ul>
<p><b>Class 11 (Lu-)</b>
</p><p>Some speakers treat words in this class as if they were in class 5/6.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<ul><li><span title="Tumbuka-language text"><i lang="tum">Lwande</i></span> = side</li>
<li><span title="Tumbuka-language text"><i lang="tum">Lumbiri</i></span> = fame</li>
<li><span title="Tumbuka-language text"><i lang="tum">Lulimi</i></span> = tongue</li></ul>
<p><b>Class 12/13 (Ka-Tu-)</b>
</p>
<ul><li><span title="Tumbuka-language text"><i lang="tum">Kanthu (kantu)</i></span> pl. <span title="Tumbuka-language text"><i lang="tum">tunthu (tuntu)</i></span> = small thing</li>
<li><span title="Tumbuka-language text"><i lang="tum">Kamwana</i></span> pl. <span title="Tumbuka-language text"><i lang="tum">tuŵana (tubana)</i></span> = baby</li>
<li><span title="Tumbuka-language text"><i lang="tum">Kayuni</i></span> pl. <span title="Tumbuka-language text"><i lang="tum">tuyuni</i></span> = bird</li>
<li><span title="Tumbuka-language text"><i lang="tum">Tulo</i></span> (no singular) = sleep</li></ul>
<p><b>Class 14/6 (U-Ma-)</b>
</p><p>These nouns are frequently abstract and have no plural.
</p>
<ul><li><span title="Tumbuka-language text"><i lang="tum">Usiku</i></span> = night</li>
<li><span title="Tumbuka-language text"><i lang="tum">Ulimi</i></span> = farming</li>
<li><span title="Tumbuka-language text"><i lang="tum">Ulalo</i></span> pl. <span title="Tumbuka-language text"><i lang="tum">maulalo</i></span> = bridge</li>
<li><span title="Tumbuka-language text"><i lang="tum">Uta</i></span> pl. <span title="Tumbuka-language text"><i lang="tum">mauta</i></span> = bow</li></ul>
<p><b>Class 15 (Ku-) Infinitive</b>
</p>
<ul><li><span title="Tumbuka-language text"><i lang="tum">Kugula</i></span> = to buy, buying</li>
<li><span title="Tumbuka-language text"><i lang="tum">Kwiba (kwibha)</i></span> = to steal, stealing</li></ul>
<p><b>Classes 16, 17, 18 (Pa-, Ku-, Mu-) Locative</b>
</p>
<ul><li><span title="Tumbuka-language text"><i lang="tum">Pasi</i></span> = underneath</li>
<li><span title="Tumbuka-language text"><i lang="tum">Kunthazi (kuntazi)</i></span> = in front, before</li>
<li><span title="Tumbuka-language text"><i lang="tum">Mukati</i></span> = inside</li></ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Concords">Concords</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tumbuka_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Concords"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Verbs, adjectives, numbers, possessives, and pronouns in Tumbuka have to agree with the noun referred to. This is done by means of prefixes, infixes, or suffixes called 'concords' which differ according to the class of noun. Class 1 has the greatest variety of concords, differing for pronouns, subject prefix, object infix, numbers, adjectives, and possessives:<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<ul><li><span title="Tumbuka-language text"><i lang="tum">Mwana u<b>yu</b></i></span> = this child</li>
<li><span title="Tumbuka-language text"><i lang="tum">Mwana <b>yu</b>moza</i></span> = one child</li>
<li><span title="Tumbuka-language text"><i lang="tum">Mwana u<b>yo</b></i></span> = that child</li>
<li><span title="Tumbuka-language text"><i lang="tum">Mwana <b>yo</b>se</i></span> = the whole child</li>
<li><span title="Tumbuka-language text"><i lang="tum">Mwana <b>wa</b>li<b>yo</b>se</i></span> = every child</li>
<li><span title="Tumbuka-language text"><i lang="tum">Mwana <b>wa</b>ka<b>mu</b>wona</i></span> = the child saw him</li>
<li><span title="Tumbuka-language text"><i lang="tum">Mwana <b>mu</b>choko (coko)</i></span> = the small child</li>
<li><span title="Tumbuka-language text"><i lang="tum">Mwana <b>wa</b> Khumbo</i></span> = Khumbo's child</li>
<li><span title="Tumbuka-language text"><i lang="tum">Mwana <b>wa</b>ne</i></span> = my child</li>
<li><span title="Tumbuka-language text"><i lang="tum">Mwana <b>wa</b>wona</i></span> = the child has seen</li></ul>
<p>Other noun classes have a smaller variety of concords, as can be seen from the table below:
</p>
<table class="wikitable" style="text-align: center; width: 200px; height: 200px;">
<caption>Table of Tumbuka concords
</caption>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Sample_phrases_and_text">Sample phrases and text</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tumbuka_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Sample phrases and text"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The following is a list of phrases that can be used when one visits a region whose primary language is Tumbuka:
</p>
<table class="wikitable">

</caption>

<th>Tumbuka

<th>English

<td>Hello

</td>
<td>hello, to a group of people
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td>Muli makola?
<p>Mwaŵa uli?
</p>
</td>
<td>how are you?
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td>Muli makola?
<p>Mwaŵa uli?
</p>
</td>
<td>How are you?, to a group of people
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td>Nili makola
</td>
<td>I'm okay
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td>Tili makola
</td>
<td>We're okay
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td>Naonga (chomene)
</td>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Verbs">Verbs</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tumbuka_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Verbs"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Subject_prefix">Subject prefix</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tumbuka_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Subject prefix"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>All verbs must have a subject prefix, which agrees with the subject noun.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> For example, the word <span title="Tumbuka-language text"><i lang="tum">ciŵinda</i></span> 'hunter' is class 7, so if it is subject, the verb has the prefix <i>ci-</i>:
</p>
<dl><dd><span title="Tumbuka-language text"><i lang="tum">ciŵinda <b>ci</b>-ka-koma nkhalamu</i></span> = 'the hunter killed a lion'<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup></dd></dl>
<p>It is also possible for the subject to be a locative noun (classes 16, 17, 18), in which case the verb has a locative prefix:<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<dl><dd><span title="Tumbuka-language text"><i lang="tum">pamphasa <b>pa</b>-ka-khala mwana</i></span> = 'on the mat there sat down a child'</dd></dl>
<p>The locative prefix <i>ku-</i> (class 17) is also used impersonally when discussing the weather:<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<dl><dd><span title="Tumbuka-language text"><i lang="tum"><b>ku</b>kuzizima madazi ghano</i></span> = 'it's cold these days'</dd></dl>
<p>When the subject is a personal pronoun, the subject prefixes are as follows (the pronoun itself may be omitted, but not the subject prefix):
</p>
<dl><dd><span title="Tumbuka-language text"><i lang="tum">(ine) <b>n</b>-kha-gula</i></span> = 'I bought' (<i>nkha-</i> stands for <i>ni-ka-</i>)</dd>
<dd><span title="Tumbuka-language text"><i lang="tum">(iwe) <b>u</b>-ka-gula</i></span> = 'you bought' (informal, singular)</dd>
<dd><span title="Tumbuka-language text"><i lang="tum">(iyo)<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup> <b>wa</b>-ka-gula</i></span> = 'he, she bought'</dd>
<dd><span title="Tumbuka-language text"><i lang="tum">(ise) <b>ti</b>-ka-gula</i></span> = 'we bought'</dd>
<dd><span title="Tumbuka-language text"><i lang="tum">(imwe) <b>mu</b>-ka-gula</i></span> = 'you bought' (plural or respectful)</dd>
<dd><span title="Tumbuka-language text"><i lang="tum">(iwo) <b>ŵa</b>-ka-gula</i></span> = 'they bought', 'he/she bought' (plural or respectful)</dd></dl>
<p>In the perfect tense, these are shortened to <span title="Tumbuka-language text"><i lang="tum">n-a-, w-a-, w-a-, t-a-, mw-a-, ŵ-a-</i></span>, e.g. <span title="Tumbuka-language text"><i lang="tum">t-a-gula</i></span> 'we have bought'.
</p><p>In <a href="/wiki/Karonga" title="Karonga">Karonga</a> dialect, in the 3rd person singular <i>a-</i> is found instead of <i>wa-</i>, and the 3rd plural is <i>wa-</i> instead of <i>ŵa-</i>, except in the perfect tense, when <i>wa-</i> and <i>ŵa-</i> are used.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Object-marker">Object-marker</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tumbuka_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Object-marker"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>To indicate the object, an infix can be added to the verb immediately before the verb root. Generally speaking, the object-marker is optional:<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<dl><dd><span title="Tumbuka-language text"><i lang="tum">Pokani wa(<b>yi</b>)gula galimoto</i></span> = 'Pokani has bought a car' (class 9)</dd>
<dd><span title="Tumbuka-language text"><i lang="tum">Changa waka(<b>mu</b>)nyamula katundu</i></span> = 'Changa carried the luggage' (class 1)</dd></dl>
<p>The object-marker agrees with the class of the object, as shown on the table of concords above.
</p><p>The object-marker can also be a locative (classes 16, 17, or 18):<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<dl><dd><span title="Tumbuka-language text"><i lang="tum">Kondwani wa(<b>pa</b>)kwera pa nyumba</i></span> = 'Kondwani has climbed on top of the house'</dd></dl>
<p>The locative markers for personal pronouns are as follows:<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<dl><dd><span title="Tumbuka-language text"><i lang="tum">wa<b>ni</b>ona (ine)</i></span> = 'he has seen me'</dd>
<dd><span title="Tumbuka-language text"><i lang="tum">wa<b>ku</b>ona (iwe)</i></span> = 'he has seen you'</dd>
<dd><span title="Tumbuka-language text"><i lang="tum">wa<b>mu</b>ona</i></span> = 'he has seen him/her'</dd>
<dd><span title="Tumbuka-language text"><i lang="tum">wa<b>ti</b>ona</i></span> = 'he has seen us'</dd>
<dd><span title="Tumbuka-language text"><i lang="tum">wa<b>mu</b>ona<b>ni</b></i></span> = 'he has seen you' (plural or respectful)</dd>
<dd><span title="Tumbuka-language text"><i lang="tum">wa<b>ŵa</b>ona</i></span> = 'he has seen them'</dd></dl>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tenses">Tenses</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tumbuka_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Tenses"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Tenses in Tumbuka are made partly by adding infixes, and partly by suffixes. Unlike Chichewa, tones do not form any part of the distinction between one tense and another.
</p><p>In the past a distinction is made between hodiernal tenses (referring to events of today) and remote tenses (referring to events of yesterday or some time ago). However, the boundary between recent and remote is not exact.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Another distinction is made between past and perfect tenses. When a perfect tense is used it carries an implication that the resulting situation still exists at the time of speaking, for example: 'the pumpkins have spread (<span title="Tumbuka-language text"><i lang="tum">zathambalala</i></span>) over the garden'.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup> The present perfect can also be used in verbs expressing a current situation such as <span title="Tumbuka-language text"><i lang="tum">ndakhala</i></span> 'I am sitting' or <span title="Tumbuka-language text"><i lang="tum">ndakondwa</i></span> 'I am pleased'. The remote perfect is used for events which happened some time ago but of which the effects still apply today, such as <span title="Tumbuka-language text"><i lang="tum">libwe lilikuwa</i></span> 'the rock has fallen' or <span title="Tumbuka-language text"><i lang="tum">walikutayika</i></span> 'he (has) died'.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The future tenses similarly distinguish near from remote events. Some tenses imply that the event will take place elsewhere, for example <span title="Tumbuka-language text"><i lang="tum">ndamukuchezga</i></span> 'I will go and visit'.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Compound tenses are also found in Tumbuka, such as <span title="Tumbuka-language text"><i lang="tum">wati wagona</i></span> 'he had slept', <span title="Tumbuka-language text"><i lang="tum">wakaŵa kuti wafumapo</i></span> 'he had just left' and <span title="Tumbuka-language text"><i lang="tum">wazamukuŵa waguliska</i></span> 'he will have sold'.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<table class="wikitable" style="text-align: left">
<caption>Some Tumbuka tenses<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup>

<p>Other future tenses are given by Vail (1972) and others.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In the 1st person singular, <i>ni-ku-</i> and <i>ni-ka-</i> are shortened to <i>nkhu-</i> and <i>nkha-</i>: <span title="Tumbuka-language text"><i lang="tum">nkhuluta</i></span> 'I am going', 'I go', <span title="Tumbuka-language text"><i lang="tum">nkhalutanga</i></span> 'I used to go'.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Negative_verbs">Negative verbs</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tumbuka_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Negative verbs"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>To make the negative of a verb in Tumbuka, the word <span title="Tumbuka-language text"><i lang="tum">yayi</i></span> or <span title="Tumbuka-language text"><i lang="tum">cha(ra)</i></span> is added at or near the end of the clause. It seems that <span title="Tumbuka-language text"><i lang="tum">yayi</i></span> is preferred by younger speakers:<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<dl><dd><span title="Tumbuka-language text"><i lang="tum">wakulemba kalata <b>yayi</b></i></span></dd>
<dd>'he is not writing a letter'</dd></dl>
<dl><dd><span title="Tumbuka-language text"><i lang="tum">tizamugwira ntchito <b>cha</b> machero</i></span></dd>
<dd>'we will not work tomorrow'</dd></dl>
<p>With the present perfect tense, however, a separate form exists, adding <i>-nda-</i> and ending in <i>-e</i>:<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<dl><dd><span title="Tumbuka-language text"><i lang="tum">enya, n<b>a</b>kumana nawo</i></span></dd>
<dd>'yes, I have met him'</dd></dl>
<dl><dd><span title="Tumbuka-language text"><i lang="tum">yayi, ni<b>nda</b>kuman<b>e</b> nawo</i></span></dd>
<dd>'no, I haven't met him'</dd></dl>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="The_Ngoni_influence_on_Tumbuka">The Ngoni influence on Tumbuka</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tumbuka_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: The Ngoni influence on Tumbuka"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p><b>Words of Ngoni (Zulu/Ndwandwe) origin found in Tumbuka:</b>
</p><p>All Tumbuka dialects have to some extent been affected by the Ngoni language, most especially in Mzimba District of Malawi. Ngoni is a language that originates from the Ndwandwe people who were neighbours to the Zulu clan prior to being conquered by the Zulu and being assimilated into the Zulu identity. The language the Ndwandwe spoke was thus nearly identical Zulu. Below are some examples of words found in chitumbuka that are of Zulu/Ndwandwe origin, though most of them have original Tumbuka counterpart words that can be used interchangeably at the speakers will, (excluding 'munwe/minwe' meaning 'finger/fingers' for example, that seemingly did not have an original counterpart or the original word has been lost). 
</p>
<table class="wikitable">

<tbody><tr>
<th>English</th>
<th>Tumbuka</th>
<th>Tumbuka-Ngoni dialect
</th></tr>
<tr>
<td>See</td>
<td>Wona</td>
<td>Bheka
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td>Smoke</td>
<td>Khweŵa</td>
<td>Bhema
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td>Man</td>
<td>Mwanalume</td>
<td>Doda
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td>Virgin</td>
<td>Mwali</td>
<td>Nthombi
</td></tr></tbody></table>

<p>An example of a folktale translated into Tumbuka and other languages of Northern Malawi is given in the Language Mapping Survey for Northern Malawi carried out by the Centre for Language Studies of the University of Malawi.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup> The Tumbuka version of the folktale goes as follows:
</p>
<dl><dd><span title="Tumbuka-language text"><span lang="tum" style="font-style: normal;">KALULU NA FULU (Citumbuka)</span></span></dd>
<dd><span title="Tumbuka-language text"><span lang="tum" style="font-style: normal;">Fulu wakaluta kukapemphiska vyakulya ku ŵanthu. Pakuyeya thumba lake wakacita kukaka ku cingwe citali na kuvwara mu singo, ndipo pakwenda thumba lake likizanga kunyuma kwakhe.</span></span></dd></dl>
<dl><dd><span title="Tumbuka-language text"><span lang="tum" style="font-style: normal;">Wali mu nthowa, kalulu wakiza kunyuma kwakhe ndipo wakati “bowo, thumba lane!” Fulu wakati, "Thumba ndane iwe, wona cingwe ici ndakaka sono nkhuguza pakwenda.” Kalulu wakakana nipera, ndipo wakati “Tilute ku Mphala yikateruzge.” Mphala yikadumula mlandu na kuceketa cingwe ico Fulu wakakakira thumba. Ŵakatola thumba lira ndipo ŵakapa kalulu.</span></span></dd></dl>
<dl><dd><span title="Tumbuka-language text"><span lang="tum" style="font-style: normal;">Pa zuŵa linyakhe Kalulu wakendanga, Fulu wakamsanga ndipo wakati, "Bowo, mcira wane!" Kalulu wakati, “Ake! Fulu iwe m'cira ngwane." Fulu wakakana, ndipo wakati, "Ndasola ngwane." Ŵakaluta ku mphala, kuti yikaŵeruzge. Ku Mphala kula mlandu ukatowera Fulu. Ŵakadumula m'cira wa Kalulu nakupa Fulu.</span></span></dd></dl>
<dl><dd>(Translation)</dd>
<dd>THE TORTOISE AND THE HARE</dd>
<dd>Tortoise went to beg food from people. To carry his bag, he tied it to a long string and wore it round his neck. As he walked along, the bag was coming behind him.</dd></dl>
<dl><dd>As he was on his way, Hare came up behind him and said, "There it is, my bag!" Tortoise said "The bag is mine, see this string I've tied now I'm pulling it as I go." Hare refused to accept this and said "Let's go the Court, so that it can judge us." The Court examined the case and cut Tortoise's string which he'd tied the bag with. They took that bag and gave it to Hare.</dd></dl>
<dl><dd>Another day when Hare was walking along, Tortoise found him and said, "There it is, my tail!" Hare said, "Nonsense, this is my tail, Tortoise." Tortoise refused to accept this and said, "What I've got is mine." They went to the Court so that it could make a judgement. In that Court, the case went in Tortoise's favour. They cut off Hare's tail and gave it to Tortoise.</dd></dl>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Some_vocabulary">Some vocabulary</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tumbuka_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Some vocabulary"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Helpful_phrases">Helpful phrases</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tumbuka_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Helpful phrases"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul><li><span title="Tumbuka-language text"><i lang="tum">Enya</i></span>    =  Yes</li>
<li><span title="Tumbuka-language text"><i lang="tum">Yayi</i></span>    =  No</li>
<li><span title="Tumbuka-language text"><i lang="tum">Yebo (yeŵo)</i></span>   =  Thank you</li>
<li><span title="Tumbuka-language text"><i lang="tum">Taonga</i></span> = We are thankful</li>
<li><span title="Tumbuka-language text"><i lang="tum">Nkhukhumba chakurya!</i></span> = I want some food&#160;!</li>
<li><span title="Tumbuka-language text"><i lang="tum">Munganipako chakurya?</i></span> = could you give me some food?</li>
<li><span title="Tumbuka-language text"><i lang="tum">Ine nkhuyowoya chiTumbuka yayi!</i></span> = I do not speak chiTumbuka!</li>
<li><span title="Tumbuka-language text"><i lang="tum">Yendani makola</i></span> = Travel well.</li>
<li><span title="Tumbuka-language text"><i lang="tum">Nkukhumba maji yakumwa</i></span> = I would like water to drink.</li></ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Greetings">Greetings</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tumbuka_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Greetings"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul><li><span title="Tumbuka-language text"><i lang="tum">Mwawuka uli?</i></span> =  Good morning.  (How did you wake up?)</li>
<li><span title="Tumbuka-language text"><i lang="tum">Tawuka makola.  Kwali imwe?</i></span> =  Fine.  And you? (I woke up well.  I don't know about you?)</li>
<li><span title="Tumbuka-language text"><i lang="tum">Muli uli?</i></span> = How are you?</li>
<li><span title="Tumbuka-language text"><i lang="tum">Nili makola, kwali imwe?</i></span> = I am fine, how are you?</li>
<li><span title="Tumbuka-language text"><i lang="tum">Mwatandala uli?</i></span>  = Good afternoon. (How did you spend the day?)</li>
<li><span title="Tumbuka-language text"><i lang="tum">Natandala makola.  Kwali imwe?</i></span> = Good afternoon.  How are you? (I spent the day well.  I don't know about you?)</li>
<li><span title="Tumbuka-language text"><i lang="tum">Monile</i></span> = somewhat more formal than "Hi". Perhaps best translated as "Greetings".</li>
<li><span title="Tumbuka-language text"><i lang="tum">Tionanenge</i></span> = We shall meet again.</li></ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="People">People</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tumbuka_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: People"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The plural ba- (ŵa-) is often used for politeness when referring to elders:
</p>
<ul><li><span title="Tumbuka-language text"><i lang="tum">Munyamata</i></span> = boy</li>
<li><span title="Tumbuka-language text"><i lang="tum">Banyamata (ŵanyamata)</i></span> = boys</li>
<li><span title="Tumbuka-language text"><i lang="tum">Musungwana</i></span> = girl</li>
<li><span title="Tumbuka-language text"><i lang="tum">Basungwana (ŵasungwana)</i></span> = girls</li>
<li><span title="Tumbuka-language text"><i lang="tum">Bamwali (ŵamwali)</i></span> = young ladies</li>
<li><span title="Tumbuka-language text"><i lang="tum">Banchembere (ŵancembele)</i></span> = a woman with babies</li>
<li><span title="Tumbuka-language text"><i lang="tum">Bamama (ŵamama)</i></span> = mother</li>
<li><span title="Tumbuka-language text"><i lang="tum">Badada(ŵadhadha)</i></span> = dad</li>
<li><span title="Tumbuka-language text"><i lang="tum">Bagogo (ŵagogo)</i></span> = grandmother</li>
<li><span title="Tumbuka-language text"><i lang="tum">Babuya (ŵabhuya)</i></span> = grandmother, also used when addressing old female persons</li>
<li><span title="Tumbuka-language text"><i lang="tum">Basekulu (ŵasekulu)</i></span> = grandfather</li>
<li><span title="Tumbuka-language text"><i lang="tum">Bankhazi (ŵankhazi)</i></span> = paternal aunt</li>
<li><span title="Tumbuka-language text"><i lang="tum">ŵa/Bamama ŵa/bachoko / ŵa/bakulu</i></span> = maternal aunt usually your mother's younger/older sister</li>
<li><span title="Tumbuka-language text"><i lang="tum">Basibweni (ŵasibweni)</i></span> = maternal uncle</li>
<li><span title="Tumbuka-language text"><i lang="tum">Badada(ŵadhadha) bachoko / bakulu</i></span> = paternal uncle usually your father's younger/older brother</li>
<li><span title="Tumbuka-language text"><i lang="tum">Mudumbu(mudhumbu) wane</i></span> = my brother/ sister (for addressing a sibling of the opposite sex)</li>
<li><span title="Tumbuka-language text"><i lang="tum">Muchoko wane / muzuna wane/ munung'una wane</i></span> = my young brother / sister (for addressing a sibling of the same sex)</li>
<li><span title="Tumbuka-language text"><i lang="tum">Mukuru wane / mulala wane</i></span> = my elder brother / sister (for addressing a sibling of the same sex)</li></ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Verbs_2">Verbs</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tumbuka_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Verbs"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul><li><span title="Tumbuka-language text"><i lang="tum">Kusebela (Kuseŵera)</i></span> = to play</li>
<li><span title="Tumbuka-language text"><i lang="tum">Kuseka</i></span> = to laugh</li>
<li><span title="Tumbuka-language text"><i lang="tum">Kurya</i></span> = to eat</li>
<li><span title="Tumbuka-language text"><i lang="tum">Kugona</i></span> = to sleep</li>
<li><span title="Tumbuka-language text"><i lang="tum">Kwenda</i></span> = to walk</li>
<li><span title="Tumbuka-language text"><i lang="tum">Kuchimbila</i></span> = to run</li>
<li><span title="Tumbuka-language text"><i lang="tum">Kulemba</i></span> = to write</li>
<li><span title="Tumbuka-language text"><i lang="tum">Kuchapa</i></span> = to do laundry</li>
<li><span title="Tumbuka-language text"><i lang="tum">Kugeza</i></span> = to bath</li>
<li><span title="Tumbuka-language text"><i lang="tum">Kuphika</i></span> = to cook</li>
<li><span title="Tumbuka-language text"><i lang="tum">Kulima</i></span> = to dig / cultivate</li>
<li><span title="Tumbuka-language text"><i lang="tum">Kupanda</i></span> = to plant</li>
<li><span title="Tumbuka-language text"><i lang="tum">Kuvina</i></span> = to dance</li>
<li><span title="Tumbuka-language text"><i lang="tum">Kwimba</i></span> = to sing</li></ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Animals">Animals</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tumbuka_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Animals"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul><li><span title="Tumbuka-language text"><i lang="tum">Fulu</i></span> = tortoise</li>
<li><span title="Tumbuka-language text"><i lang="tum">Kalulu</i></span> = hare</li>
<li><span title="Tumbuka-language text"><i lang="tum">Gwere</i></span> = hippo</li>
<li><span title="Tumbuka-language text"><i lang="tum">Chimbwi</i></span> = hyena</li>
<li><span title="Tumbuka-language text"><i lang="tum">Njoka</i></span> = snake</li>
<li><span title="Tumbuka-language text"><i lang="tum">Nkhumba</i></span> = pig</li>
<li><span title="Tumbuka-language text"><i lang="tum">Ng'ombe</i></span> = cow</li>
<li><span title="Tumbuka-language text"><i lang="tum">Nchebe (Ncheŵe)</i></span> = dog</li>
<li><span title="Tumbuka-language text"><i lang="tum">Chona/pusi/kiti</i></span> = cat</li>
<li><span title="Tumbuka-language text"><i lang="tum">Mbelele</i></span> = sheep</li>
<li><span title="Tumbuka-language text"><i lang="tum">Nkalamu</i></span> = lion</li>
<li><span title="Tumbuka-language text"><i lang="tum">Mbuzi</i></span> = goat</li>
<li><span title="Tumbuka-language text"><i lang="tum">Nkhuku</i></span> = chicken</li></ul>

<li>Vail, Hazen Leroy (1971). "The noun classes of Tumbuka". <i>African studies</i>, v. 30, 1, p.&#160;35-59.</li>
<li>Vail, Hazen Leroy (1972). "Aspects of the Tumbuka Verb". Ph.D. dissertation, University of Wisconsin.</li></ul>
</div>

<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1134653256">.mw-parser-output .side-box{margin:4px 0;box-sizing:border-box;border:1px solid #aaa;font-size:88%;line-height:1.25em;background-color:#f9f9f9;display:flow-root}.mw-parser-output .side-box-abovebelow,.mw-parser-output .side-box-text{padding:0.25em 0.9em}.mw-parser-output .side-box-image{padding:2px 0 2px 0.9em;text-align:center}.mw-parser-output .side-box-imageright{padding:2px 0.9em 2px 0;text-align:center}@media(min-width:500px){.mw-parser-output .side-box-flex{display:flex;align-items:center}.mw-parser-output .side-box-text{flex:1}}@media(min-width:720px){.mw-parser-output .side-box{width:238px}.mw-parser-output .side-box-right{clear:right;float:right;margin-left:1em}.mw-parser-output .side-box-left{margin-right:1em}}</style><div class="side-box side-box-right plainlinks sistersitebox"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1126788409">

<div class="side-box-image"><span class="noviewer" typeof="mw:File"><span><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/8/80/Wikipedia-logo-v2.svg/40px-Wikipedia-logo-v2.svg.png" decoding="async" width="40" height="37" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/8/80/Wikipedia-logo-v2.svg/60px-Wikipedia-logo-v2.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/8/80/Wikipedia-logo-v2.svg/80px-Wikipedia-logo-v2.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="103" data-file-height="94" /></span></span></div>

<div class="side-box-image"><span class="noviewer" typeof="mw:File"><span><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/Wikivoyage-Logo-v3-icon.svg/40px-Wikivoyage-Logo-v3-icon.svg.png" decoding="async" width="40" height="40" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/Wikivoyage-Logo-v3-icon.svg/60px-Wikivoyage-Logo-v3-icon.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/Wikivoyage-Logo-v3-icon.svg/80px-Wikivoyage-Logo-v3-icon.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="193" data-file-height="193" /></span></span></div>

class="nowraplinks mw-collapsible mw-collapsed navbox-subgroup" style="border-spacing:0"><tbody><tr><th scope="col" class="navbox-title" colspan="2" style=";font-weight:normal;"><div id="Zones_A_–_B" navbox-list navbox-odd" style="width:100%;padding:0"><div style="padding:0 0.25em"></div><table class="nowraplinks navbox-subgroup" style="border-spacing:0"><tbody><tr><th scope="row"
